  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3299422" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/205885-dan-martin" class="left imgcol" title="Dan Martin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1196836690p2/205885.jpg" alt="Dan Martin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/3299422?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 19, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/205885-dan-martin" class="user" title="Dan Martin">Dan Martin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer3299422">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10701819458790385518">The first thing you have to know about this series, and this is the real pivotal point in whether you want to read them or not, is that Thomas Coveenant is NOT A HERO. Like, in any sense. There are a couple really fantastic heroes in this book, but all of the chapters in the 1st book, and the majority thereafter all center around covenant, the unbeliever. <br />The story of the book is honestly a little trite. An evil lord threatening a beautiful land. Covenenant has an important ring. <br />But! Thomas, oh</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10701819458790385518">The first thing you have to know about this series, and this is the real pivotal point in whether you want to read them or not, is that Thomas Coveenant is NOT A HERO. Like, in any sense. There are a couple really fantastic heroes in this book, but all of the chapters in the 1st book, and the majority thereafter all center around covenant, the unbeliever. <br />The story of the book is honestly a little trite. An evil lord threatening a beautiful land. Covenenant has an important ring. <br />But! Thomas, oh thomas. He's jealous, bitter, frustrated, cynical -- you want to criticize him for not being all heroic and shit, but... there's good reasons for him not to be. <br />**spoilers (barely, almost what you get off the back cover)** <br />Thomas covenant is a leper. A famous author who had it all, and lost it instantly. So, he's tossed into this imaginary world where disease isn't even a concept-- so what does he do? Just believe in it? It's not like, "lucky you, you're healthy!" He figures if he does, the second he wakes back up, as a leper, outcast, unclean , and alone, he would kill himself. Put yourself in his shoes here~ So that's the premise of the story; and it's good. Just accept him as a poor, incredibly unfortunate leper, not as a hero, and you'll like it.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_53110400">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53110400" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1713956-manny" class="left imgcol" title="Manny"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442491692p2/1713956.jpg" alt="Manny" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/53110400?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 18, 2009</a>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer53110400">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18093096170430968271">A Swedish friend told me I just had to read this series - it was like Tolkien but better. I borrowed the first three, and dutifully read them, waiting for the point to dawn. It never did. Tolkien, to me, is all about the language and the names, and Donaldson's names ranged between uninspired and downright moronic. ("Berek Halfhand". Bleah.) It just grated.<br /><br />To add insult to injury, I managed to drop one volume into the bath while reading it, so I had to buy a new copy to return to him. I've not lo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18093096170430968271">A Swedish friend told me I just had to read this series - it was like Tolkien but better. I borrowed the first three, and dutifully read them, waiting for the point to dawn. It never did. Tolkien, to me, is all about the language and the names, and Donaldson's names ranged between uninspired and downright moronic. ("Berek Halfhand". Bleah.) It just grated.<br /><br />To add insult to injury, I managed to drop one volume into the bath while reading it, so I had to buy a new copy to return to him. I've not looked at Donaldson since.<br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_641535974">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/641535974" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny" class="left imgcol" title="Evgeny"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1349810697p2/9340136.jpg" alt="Evgeny" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/641535974?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 12, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny" class="user" title="Evgeny">Evgeny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer641535974">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1495801409568252292">Thomas Covenant had it all: a good family, his first book was a New York Times bestseller, his second book was in the progress. Suddenly he developed leprosy, his wife left him taking his son with her, people avoid any kind of contact with him turning him into a self-loathing bitter whining person. He is a leper outcast unclean.<br /><br />Some high powers brought him to magic land where he is destined to either help fight Great Evil, or destroy everything - the choice is his. The problem is: he does not re</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1495801409568252292">Thomas Covenant had it all: a good family, his first book was a New York Times bestseller, his second book was in the progress. Suddenly he developed leprosy, his wife left him taking his son with her, people avoid any kind of contact with him turning him into a self-loathing bitter whining person. He is a leper outcast unclean.<br /><br />Some high powers brought him to magic land where he is destined to either help fight Great Evil, or destroy everything - the choice is his. The problem is: he does not really believe the land is real - this is only his mind affected by his leprosy which plays tricks on him. As a result he does not really care about the Land (this is an actual name of the place) or its inhabitants. He is a leper outcast unclean.<br /><br />This is my second attempt to read the series. The first time I read it, I was really put off by one of Covenant's actions in the Land - people who read this know what I talk about. Still considering the fact that a lot of people call this the best fantasy ever I was curious to finish this. Oh, in case you forgot: Thomas Covenant is a leper outcast unclean.<br /><br />Now that I finally finished the book, I am underwhelmed. The most GR ratings for it are either 5 stars or 1 star. I guess I will be in minority with my rating. I found this book to be a slightly above average Tolkien clone with a very unlikable protagonist. After all, he is a leper outcast unclean.<br /><br />Quite a few of the scenes can be easily attributed to Tolkien's classic with simple change of names. Thomas Covenant has a ring with unknown great powers - does this ring a bell? Sorry for a bad unintended pun. He needs to get to <s> Rivendell </s>, sorry I mean Lord's Keep from where <s> The Fellowship of the Ring </s>, sorry Quest is formed from different people. I can go on and on, but will stop here to avoid further spoilers. The only really original part is that the main character is a leper outcast unclean.<br /><br />The book was probably shocking in the time it was written, but if one compares it to modern fantasy, it is very mild - with the exception of the scene I already mentioned, but even that is not THAT shocking nowadays; it just strengthens reader's revulsion for Thomas Covenant who is a leper outcast unclean.<br /><br />Speaking of the main character - he is NOT an anti-hero as some readers call him. For good examples of anti-heroes, please refer to Elric by <a title="Michael Moorcock" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16939.Michael_Moorcock">Michael Moorcock</a>, Lady from <a title="Chronicles of the Black Company (The Chronicles of the Black Company, #1-3) by Glen Cook" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/400924.Chronicles_of_the_Black_Company__The_Chronicles_of_the_Black_Company___1_3_">Chronicles of the Black Company</a>, Gerald Tarrant from <a title="Black Sun Rising (The Coldfire Trilogy, #1) by C.S. Friedman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36159.Black_Sun_Rising__The_Coldfire_Trilogy___1_">Black Sun Rising</a>, or countless others. Thomas Covenant is just a whining jerk (and something worse which I will not mention here as it will give a spoiler). I know quite a few real-life people who had it as bad as or even worse than him, but they managed to remain good humans; Thomas Covenant is a very pitiful excuse for a human being. He is a leper outcast unclean.<br /><br />Did you notice that I never mention anybody except for the main character? The reason for this is that every single person in the Land is a typical Mary Sue without any exceptions, and thus are fairly indistinguishable from each other and not very interesting, except for a leper outcast unclean character.<br /><br />I thought about giving 2 star rating to this book, but the very end was interesting enough to warrant an extra star: after all, I would not read the next book in the series with the first one having just 2 stars. In this case this book was good enough for me to proceed to the next one even though Thomas Covenant is a leper outcast unclean.<br /><br />One last note: if you think I overdid on the whole leper outcast unclean thing - Thomas Covenant calls himself like this at least once per page if not more often, so if somebody wants to read this for the first time, get used to it. He keeps whining like this non-stop. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1495801409568252292">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer3350076">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14805930673033049433">Another series I did in one long weekend, this was probably one of the most influential series I read during high school. For some reason I absolutely hated the main character Thomas Conevenant (probably because he was an ass) and my one driving passion was to keep reading until he was killed off. Until of course the last book in the second series where I got over it and decided he should live and then he was killed off. <br /><br />As an interesting aside, this series made it remarkably less likely that I</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14805930673033049433">Another series I did in one long weekend, this was probably one of the most influential series I read during high school. For some reason I absolutely hated the main character Thomas Conevenant (probably because he was an ass) and my one driving passion was to keep reading until he was killed off. Until of course the last book in the second series where I got over it and decided he should live and then he was killed off. <br /><br />As an interesting aside, this series made it remarkably less likely that I would have committed suicide since whenever I thought about it, I would promise myself I would first take out Stephon Donaldson before I did, the thought of which tended to make me somewhat happier at the time.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_9493182">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9493182" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/467795-michael" class="left imgcol" title="Michael"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1191548046p2/467795.jpg" alt="Michael" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/9493182?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 24, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/467795-michael" class="user" title="Michael">Michael</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer9493182">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8884395268630459126">At first I wasn't sure that I liked this novel. I had a hard time with the idea that Thomas Covenant is the ultimate anti-hero, with none of the redeeming qualities of an average anti-hero. He is a sniveling, irritating, coward who has to be prodded every step of the way. The only thing that makes him likable is that he is acting in a very human way in a very inhuman circumstance. I had to let go of wanting Covenant to shape and act like a hero. I am looking forward to the rest of the series. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_717901639">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/717901639" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5743748-wastrel" class="left imgcol" title="Wastrel"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1317660831p2/5743748.jpg" alt="Wastrel" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/717901639?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 18, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5743748-wastrel" class="user" title="Wastrel">Wastrel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/546307.Lord_Foul_s_Bane" title="Paperback 9780345314147" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5743748-wastrel?shelf=z-2015" class="actionLinkLite">z-2015</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5743748-wastrel?shelf=fantastika-neoromantic-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantastika-neoromantic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer717901639">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3026520784186353027">Well that started off a lot better than I thought it might. And it ended... a lot worse than I hoped it might.<br /><br />My full (and this one is very full!) review can be found <a rel="nofollow" href="https://vacuouswastrel.wordpress.com/2015/01/27/lord-fouls-bane-by-stephen-r-donaldson/">over on my blog</a>.<br /><br />However, the brief summary version would be: this is a fascinating Calvinist (though the author left the faith of his parents) reimagining of Tolkienian neo-Romantic fantasy, with a rich (but in my opinion not yet absurd) use of language, dozens of fantastic lines, and a deep and calculated ideological-theological s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3026520784186353027">Well that started off a lot better than I thought it might. And it ended... a lot worse than I hoped it might.<br /><br />My full (and this one is very full!) review can be found <a rel="nofollow" href="https://vacuouswastrel.wordpress.com/2015/01/27/lord-fouls-bane-by-stephen-r-donaldson/">over on my blog</a>.<br /><br />However, the brief summary version would be: this is a fascinating Calvinist (though the author left the faith of his parents) reimagining of Tolkienian neo-Romantic fantasy, with a rich (but in my opinion not yet absurd) use of language, dozens of fantastic lines, and a deep and calculated ideological-theological symbolism. It's also a consistently individual vision (despite superficial tropes of the genre) and continually makes impressively bold choices on language use, imagery, characterisation, plot, pacing, symbolism, and frankly every dimension possible. <br /><br />It's also clunky and unadroit; the author is unable to change his narrative voice and presentational style to match the demands of his content, so what works as powerful in the big scenes becomes leaden and ponderous in the preparatory sections. Far too much of the book is spent on people moving from one place to another with relatively little incident, and on long expositionary monologues by villains and heroes alike.<br /><br />The manuscript was originally rejected 47 times, by every single publisher in America. And I can completely understand why.<br /><br />It went on to sell millions of copies, help to create the commercial fantasy genre, and gain legions of fanatically devoted fans around the world. And I can completely understand that too.<br /><br />It's a better book to have read than to actually be reading, and it also tends to provoke love-it-or-hate-it responses. But if you can overcome any revulsions to the mature content (trigger warning: if you have triggers, they will at some point be triggered by the Covenant books; these things get seriously nightmarish at times, though this first one is relatively mild, apart from That One Thing), and if you can put aside any natural tendency to laugh at, say, evil maniacal laughter or use of archaic vocabulary, or at Everything Being So Serious All The Time, then this series is not only a seminal landmark in the history of the fantasy genre but also a genuinely interesting literary work of a kind that just doesn't get published anymore. <br /><br />I'm calling it 'Not Bad' rather than 'Good', though it's really more a blend of some very good things and some very bad things all in one. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3026520784186353027">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_8308062">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8308062" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/581920-thomas" class="left imgcol" title="Thomas"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442457403p2/581920.jpg" alt="Thomas" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/8308062?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 27, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/581920-thomas" class="user" title="Thomas">Thomas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/581920-thomas?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer8308062">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2284849803708239102">Warning: Readers should not expect the main character to show up, draw a magic scimitar or lightsaber, and slice through the enemy. In this series, the bad guys are just part of Thomas Covenant's problem. He is also fighting enemies within himself. Be prepared to feel troubled over his plight and occasionally frustrated by his unwillingness to accept his situation and to fight. There's still plenty of excitement and all the elements of well crafted fantasy. But there's so much more.</span>

          </span>

      <span id="like_container_review_8308062" class="likeItContainer"><a href="/rating/voters/8308062?resource_type=Review" rel="nofollow" id="like_count_review_8308062"><span class="likesCount">9 likes</span></a> · <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F219205.Lord_Foul_s_Bane" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" rel="nofollow">Like</a></span> · <a href="/review/show/8308062?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1">see review</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_612999534">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/612999534" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/20264323-jason-olson" class="left imgcol" title="Jason Olson"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Jason Olson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/612999534?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 11, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/20264323-jason-olson" class="user" title="Jason Olson">Jason Olson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer612999534">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12790517775610462991">I read this book when I was in 5th or 6th grade. I had just read lord of the rings, and I was searching through my dad's books for something else to read and I found this... <br /><br />I remember thinking at the time that for as much as I liked the LOTR, the bad guys just weren't bad enough. The good guys were a little too good. For as much as I loved middle earth, I felt like the world Tolkien built was much grander and complex than the characters that inhabited it. <br /><br />Lord Foul's Bane answered those issues</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12790517775610462991">I read this book when I was in 5th or 6th grade. I had just read lord of the rings, and I was searching through my dad's books for something else to read and I found this... <br /><br />I remember thinking at the time that for as much as I liked the LOTR, the bad guys just weren't bad enough. The good guys were a little too good. For as much as I loved middle earth, I felt like the world Tolkien built was much grander and complex than the characters that inhabited it. <br /><br />Lord Foul's Bane answered those issues and then some. Maybe a little too much for what I was expecting. I immediately liked the tone of the writing. I didn't really notice the vocabulary that was way above my head, I felt like I understood the words in context. (Although I was probably dead wrong about that) Still, it didn't diminish the read for me, it added to the character of the world somehow. Especially the colors: argent, vermillion, azure...<br /><br />At the time, I liked books for the escape. I suppose I liked to live vicariously through the heroes. So when I started this book, I couldn't wait to get to the fantasy part. When I did, I was immediately taken in by the land. I was sympathetic to the main character, and everything seemed to be lining up for a great fantasy ride.<br /><br />If you have read the books, then you already know that Thomas Covenant will shortly screw up anything and everything for me. He is NOT up for a thrilling fantasy ride. He's not even up for some common courtesy. The people of the land, and the land itself, seems better and more vivid than our world by far. It was for them I kept reading, and shaking my head at this total bastard of a main character. <br /><br />So why the 5 stars? Because this series has the best world of any book I have ever read. Lord Foul is a great bad guy, so much better than Sauron. I always thought Sauron overlooking the hobbits going to mount doom was kind of dumb. I remember the reasoning Gandalf gave, but no contigency planning? Not even 100 or so gaurds watching the only entrance to Mount Doom day and night? Lord Foul was always ten steps ahead of the mere mortals, the obstacles he put in front of the heroes seemed insurmountable. Even their victories seem hopeless. I love how intelligent and cruel and disdainful he is. Just a great bad guy, and somehow you have to respect him. <br /><br />So the world is awesome, and the bad guy is awesome. I'm no expert, but the writing itself made everything seem very vivid. The wounds are brutal, the beauty of the land comes through the pages, you care about all of the characters in the book, even the total bastard that is Thomas Covenant. So the writing is awesome. I have read some reviews where people fixate on a word (like "clenched") that gets overused, but I never noticed. If your sufficiently caught up in the story, I don't think your mind will even be working like that. (For me at least, a book is like movie and I hardly notice the words themselves, they just fly by my eyes and the movie plays in my head, so I would probably be a terrible editor).<br /><br />So is there any bad? The story really drags for me during the journey with Atarian. After what happened to Lena, the whole thing is extremely uncomfortable, and the continued lack of heroics from our "hero" just puts you off more and more. In hindsight, this journey is extremely important to the entire series. So its not really bad, but upon re-reading the book (many times in the years since) I find myself skimming through until we meet foamfollower. The journey with Atarian is necessary and important, but it might be a journey many readers do not make it through if they are already put off by the book. Not technically bad, more of a necessary low point I think. <br /><br />The book really picks up when we meet foamfollower. And I even start to like Covenant for the first time. He shows a glimmer of not being a complete puke. Revelstone, the bloodgaurd, and the lords are awesome. The journey to recover Kevins lore was much more like the LOTR-but-more-serious adventure I had been hoping for. Thomas of course lets me down in the end, and I go away still shaking my head at the guy. <br /><br />Maybe I was a strange 5th grader, but after finishing this book, I immediately started the 2nd one. I give this book 5 stars because I still pick it up and start the entire chronices over every few years. I feel like I know Foamfollower and Mhoram, and of course, Thomas Covenant. I've read a dozen Drizzt books and can't say I really feel like I know or care about the guy. The morals of most fantasy character seem pure and fairly transparant. (Although Raistlin from the Dragonlance series was pretty great.) Of all the hobbits, only Samwise seemed to have a distinct character (He was alot funnier in the books). Aragorn, Legolas, Gimli, all seemed kind of the same. Good guys with a different body type and background. <br /><br />Most character I leave behind when I put a book down, but the characters of the land stay with me for some reason, especially from the first chronicles. Foamfollower, Mhoram, Lena, Elena, Thomas Covenant, Lord Foul, all stick with me. The land is the only fantasy world that actually seems like it's worth sacrificing yourself for. So yeah, 5 stars, and I would recommend everyone read it at some point, even though the journey is not always easy!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12790517775610462991">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1393156253">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1393156253" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/21982745-sumant" class="left imgcol" title="Sumant"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1373196404p2/21982745.jpg" alt="Sumant" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1393156253?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 25, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/21982745-sumant" class="user" title="Sumant">Sumant</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/21982745-sumant?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21982745-sumant?shelf=chronicles-of-thomas-covenant" class="actionLinkLite">chronicles-of-thomas-covenant</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1393156253">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13049313131136865131">I had read a lot of positive and an equal number of negative reviews of this series, so finally I decided to take a plunge into this series. After finishing first book of <em>Chronicles of Thomas Covenant</em> I am basically undecided as to how to rate this book, because neither is the book fantastic nor is it that bad to stop reading the series altogether. <br /><br />Some of the strong points of the book are<br /><br /><em>Donaldson's paints a pretty picture of Land.</em><br /><em>Different races in Land.</em><br /><br />Some of the weak points of the book are<br /><br /><em>C</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13049313131136865131">I had read a lot of positive and an equal number of negative reviews of this series, so finally I decided to take a plunge into this series. After finishing first book of <em>Chronicles of Thomas Covenant</em> I am basically undecided as to how to rate this book, because neither is the book fantastic nor is it that bad to stop reading the series altogether. <br /><br />Some of the strong points of the book are<br /><br /><em>Donaldson's paints a pretty picture of Land.</em><br /><em>Different races in Land.</em><br /><br />Some of the weak points of the book are<br /><br /><em>Covenant tests your patience.</em><br /><br />Let me elaborate on the above points now<br /><br /><em>Donaldson's paints a pretty picture of Land.</em><br /><br />The story is about an author <em>Thomas covenant</em> whose last book was a best seller and who finds himself at the peak of his life, but things soon start falling apart of him when he is diagnosed with leprosy. His wife divorces him fearing the disease will affect their son and the town people shun him from even normal activities like paying bills. <em>Covenant</em> manages to survive due the training he has got in leprosy clinic, one day his mental nerve breaks and he decides to go into the town to confront the people regarding his out-casting.<br /><br />On the way to bank he meets with an accident and gets transported to a magical <strong>Land</strong>, he learns that he has been summoned by a power who gives him a message to take to the lords of the land that their power over the land is soon going to end. The book should be read for the descriptions of <strong>Land</strong>, it is a place where mud has medicinal powers and which even heals <em>Covenant's</em> leprosy. During his journey to lord's keep i.e. <strong>Revelstone</strong> he encounters a wide variety of people of land.<br /><br /><em>Different races in Land.</em><br /><br />Some of the different races in the land are<br /><br />1.<em>Stone downers</em><br /><br />These people help <em>Covenant</em> in the first phase of his journey, and they are basically the people who try to find bigger picture in stones, they have belief that the stones are a part of something bigger and they try to fit it into original shape. They also know a lot about medicinal properties of land.<br /><br />2.<em>Wood havenen</em><br /><br />These people basically dwell on a huge tree, and it is here where <em>Covenant</em>gets himself a staff from one of their lords.<br /><br />3.<em>Giants</em><br /><br />Giants here are basically lost people who have made the <strong>Land</strong> as their temporary abode, they are on a quest to find their dwelling place which they have forgotten through their generations. The <em>giants</em> are also one of the long lived races in the <strong>Land</strong>. <br /><br />4.<em>Haruchai</em><br /><br />They are the ones who have dedicated their lives in the service of the lords of the land, at any time we have five hundred of them present at <strong>revelstone</strong> guarding the lords. They also ride magical creatures called as the <strong>ranyhyn</strong>.<br /><br /><em>Donaldson</em> borrows a lot from <em>Lord of the rings</em> with only difference being <em>Covenant</em> as a sort of anti hero who manages to scowl even when something good happens to him. This really makes him an irritating character to read.<br /><br /><em>Covenant tests your patience.</em><br /><br /><em>Covenant</em> is a leper,outcast and unclean but not a single page of the book passes where he does not have this dialogue with himself, it feels like instead of <em>Covenant's</em> physical body it is his mind which is withering away with leprosy. He constantly scowls at everything and everyone and refuses to believe in himself due to his leprosy.<br /><br />I think <em>Donaldson</em> overdoes the leprosy angle with <em>Covenant</em> because constant ramble of the main protagonist left me irritated with him. We can expect a person who has been shunned by society to be mentally unstable person, but <em>Covenant</em> even behaves badly with people who support him and this constant behavior left me irritated. I give this book 3/5 stars. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13049313131136865131">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_126498589">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126498589" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1436646-ethan" class="left imgcol" title="Ethan"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Ethan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/126498589?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 16, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1436646-ethan" class="user" title="Ethan">Ethan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer126498589">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10794396843933872245">This book hasn’t aged well. Perhaps back in 1978 when it was published, it was amazing and interesting because there was nothing to compare it to. Unfortunately, the world has moved on and left this poor guy in the back of the used bookstore, where he sits and twiddles his dusty laurels and hopes for some sucker to read him. That sucker was me.<br /><br />Minor spoilers here, so turn away if you must, but honestly I don’t think it will alter the reading experience a whole lot…so here goes.<br /><br />The main character</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10794396843933872245">This book hasn’t aged well. Perhaps back in 1978 when it was published, it was amazing and interesting because there was nothing to compare it to. Unfortunately, the world has moved on and left this poor guy in the back of the used bookstore, where he sits and twiddles his dusty laurels and hopes for some sucker to read him. That sucker was me.<br /><br />Minor spoilers here, so turn away if you must, but honestly I don’t think it will alter the reading experience a whole lot…so here goes.<br /><br />The main character is lame. Pretty much 100% lame. He’s grumpy, self-pitying, nonsensical, unsympathetic, kind of stupid, and incredibly boring. He does really idiotic things. In the beginning of the book, he spontaneously rapes a chick who’s befriended him (my brother had courteously informed me that it was going to happen, otherwise I might have chucked the book in the garbage bin when I hit that part). Later on, he decides to starve himself (still can’t figure out what that’s all about: a hunger strike in the middle of an epic journey just seems like a stupid idea). Every so often, he does something amazing for no particular reason, and people get all excited and kiss his feet (in response, he just growls and spits on them, since that’s what he does). Things tend to explode a lot when he hits them with sticks. His claim to fame is a white gold ring, his wedding band, and I could care less. He tends to be angry a lot. At one point in the book, he comes out of a river or something, and drips water angrily on the ground. He’s that angry! I’m not sure why. This guy is supposedly the best anti-hero ever, but he’s really not a hero at all. He’s just anti.<br /><br />The world is…lame. Huge and epic? Maybe back in 1978. But not anymore, bud: today’s fantasy writers would eat your entire world for breakfast and ask for a second helping. And there are just too many similarities to Tolkien for me. The idea of (the laughably named) Lord Foul is far too close to Sauron-Morgoth. There’s a powerful ring (at one point a cavewight tries to bite the ring off Covenant’s finger—how’s that for déjà vu?) and a Company of fellows who are on their way to accomplish some Quest. There’s even a big mountain (read Mount Doom) for them to Quest their way towards. Maybe the present-day character in a medieval world was something of a novelty, but it, too, has been done and done again, and I never was a bit fan of A Connecticut Yankee in King Arthur’s Court anyway.<br /><br />The other characters in the book are just plain strange and unsympathetic. Between the unfortunately-named Ramen (my favorite college snack) with their smarty-pants horses, and the vaguely Entish giant who seems to sing at every opportunity, I just couldn’t work up enough interest to care if they lived or died. When you actually WANT a character to die, is that bad? I wanted a lot of characters to die.<br /><br />The writing is horrible. Someone here mentioned purple prose. Maybe that’s not quite right. The prose is the color of curdled blood, reeking of wrongness, emitting a light that shines luridly in a grotesque parody of real prose, beating down the spirit like some terrible ur-thing that devours the souls of mortal men and hurls them, quivering with exhaustion, away from this book. So my last sentence is an attempt to duplicate this goofball’s writing style.<br /><br />The book is supposed to be fast-paced. Again, maybe in 1978, this was a wild ride. But now, in the age of Google and the half-second attention span, this thing can’t cut the mustard. I found the extensive description of traveling scenery to be a bit boring. There were a few interesting moments, but the problem is that there weren’t enough to actually keep my attention.<br /><br />Donaldson's Wikipedia entry, if it is to be believed, says that this book had been turned down by four dozen publishers. I can see why.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10794396843933872245">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10008244908726508296">First of the Thomas Covenant series. My husband remembers this was all the rage in 1976. I started reading this series much later. Everywhere I went with this book people told me they had read it and how good it was. I was doubtful at first but my roommate's boyfriend told me it got off to a slow start but not to give up. He said it was worth it to keep reading and boy, was he right! I think Stephen R. Donaldson became a better writer as he went through this series. I had read a couple of his la</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10008244908726508296">First of the Thomas Covenant series. My husband remembers this was all the rage in 1976. I started reading this series much later. Everywhere I went with this book people told me they had read it and how good it was. I was doubtful at first but my roommate's boyfriend told me it got off to a slow start but not to give up. He said it was worth it to keep reading and boy, was he right! I think Stephen R. Donaldson became a better writer as he went through this series. I had read a couple of his later books before I started this series and that was what prompted me to attempt this. This series moved me and gave me a lot to think about, not to mention being such a good story.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1300465035">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1300465035" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/43393414-murkypoke" class="left imgcol" title="Murkypoke"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1432718357p2/43393414.jpg" alt="Murkypoke" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1300465035?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 06, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/43393414-murkypoke" class="user" title="Murkypoke">Murkypoke</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1300465035">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6443141207904125540">LORD FOUL’S BANE by Stephen R. Donaldson is one of the most boring and most disappointing books I have read in my life. It has been oft recommended to me and spoken of as if it were a classic. I do not recommend you read this book and the only thing it is a classic for is how not to write.<br /><br />For a start Donaldson suffers from chronic over-figuration. As if, as though, as if, as though over and over again and again. The book could be halved, yes halved!, if the stupidly irrelevant, distracting, pond</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6443141207904125540">LORD FOUL’S BANE by Stephen R. Donaldson is one of the most boring and most disappointing books I have read in my life. It has been oft recommended to me and spoken of as if it were a classic. I do not recommend you read this book and the only thing it is a classic for is how not to write.<br /><br />For a start Donaldson suffers from chronic over-figuration. As if, as though, as if, as though over and over again and again. The book could be halved, yes halved!, if the stupidly irrelevant, distracting, ponderous and self-indulgent figurative language were simply cut. The problem then would be the half that remained.<br /><br />Nothing happens in LORD FOUL’S BANE. Nothing. The Unbeliever travels from point A to point B and predictably uninteresting things happen to him along the way. I repeatedly found myself wondering why nothing was happening and wondering why I was still reading even as my mind wandered off into its own far more interesting thoughts. I became the real Unbeliever, as in I can’t believe I’m still reading this junk.<br /><br />LORD FOUL’S BANE is simply dated, badly dated. It reads like it should be deleted form all databases, pulped and forgotten about. It is old fashioned writing that has a single saving grace, it is brilliant to cure insomnia.<br /><br />Avoid LORD FOUL’S BANE like it has leprosy. You won’t even miss it.<br /><br />By awarding LORD FOUL’S BANE one star I mean only one thing, under no circumstances bother reading this book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6443141207904125540">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UMo0W2LXmOUzhRTyBikXl+L3ec0cEXwUqxquBBKNZWU1HguIkAWMH79dYEl4SPElqwC61FXMO77BE6uW3hiTIA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

It sounds like the worst sort of hackneyed formula romance. Think again, for &amp;quot;A Man of His Word&amp;quot; may well be the most original fantasy you ever read. The magic is unique and applied in unexpected ways, some of which the late Lester del Rey admitted he had not met in fifty years as writer and editor. The world itself is unique - there are no humans in Pandemia, only imps, elves, gnomes, jotnar, and many more, all of whom you will recognize as &amp;quot;human.&amp;quot;\n\nIn MAGIC CASEMENT the tale begins gently, even slowly, with Inosolan enjoying an idyllic childhood in her father\'s tiny backwater kingdom, too innocent even to understand that the feelings she shares with her friend Rap are more than friendship. Mystery, menace, and the gods appear in short order, and from then on the story grows in scope and power to straddle the world, and adversity thrusts rapid maturity on Rap and Inos.       <a href="/author/show/12980.Stephen_R_Donaldson"><img alt="12980" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1425823085p2/12980.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer3647840310683227848">Stephen Reeder Donaldson is an American fantasy, science fiction, and mystery novelist; in the United Kingdom he is usually called "Stephen Donaldson" (without the "R"). He has also written non-fiction under the pen name Reed Stephens.<br /><br />EARLY LIFE AND EDUCATION:<br /><br />Stephen R. Donaldson was born May 13, 1947 in Cleveland, Ohio. His father, James, was a medical missionary and his mother, Ruth, a prostheti</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3647840310683227848">Stephen Reeder Donaldson is an American fantasy, science fiction, and mystery novelist; in the United Kingdom he is usually called "Stephen Donaldson" (without the "R"). He has also written non-fiction under the pen name Reed Stephens.<br /><br />EARLY LIFE AND EDUCATION:<br /><br />Stephen R. Donaldson was born May 13, 1947 in Cleveland, Ohio. His father, James, was a medical missionary and his mother, Ruth, a prosthetist (a person skilled in making or fitting prosthetic devices). Donaldson spent the years between the ages of 3 and 16 living in India, where his father was working as an orthopaedic surgeon. Donaldson earned his bachelor's degree from The College of Wooster and master's degree from Kent State University. <br /><br />INSPIRATIONS:<br /><br />Donaldson's work is heavily influenced by other fantasy authors such as J.R.R. Tolkien, Roger Zelazny, Joseph Conrad, Henry James, and William Faulkner. The writers he most admires are Patricia A. McKillip, Steven Erikson, and Tim Powers.<br /><br />It is believed that a speech his father made on leprosy (whilst working with lepers in India) led to Donaldson's creation of Thomas Covenant, the anti-hero of his most famous work (Thomas Covenant). The first book in that series, <em>Lord Foul's Bane</em>, received 47 rejections before a publisher agreed to publish it.<br /><br />PROMINENT WORK:<br />Stephen Donaldson came to prominence in 1977 with the The Chronicles of Thomas Covenant, which is centred around a leper shunned by society and his trials and tribulations as his destiny unfolds. These books established Donaldson as one of the most important figures in modern fantasy fiction.<br /><br />PERSONAL LIFE:<br />He currently resides in New Mexico.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.stephendonaldson.com/fromtheauthor/gi.php">THE GRADUAL INTERVIEW</a><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3647840310683227848">...more</a>

    </div>
